<rating>3< /rating>< review>
Most of the wine is not estate grown and personally that is something that interests me in local wine tasting . The one estate grown variety was our favorite on the tasting menu. Our server was very friendly and a breath of fresh air. The owner stopped by and visited our table, which was very nice. The tasting includes crackers and chocolate, however there was not a wine that really stood out to us. The tasting area was a bit 'busy' feeling even though we were one of the only ones there.< /review>

Recently visited a lot of the local wineries in the Ramona area and we came across this one. One of the most accommodating wineries there is. Their tastings comes with a good amount of samples + complimentary chocolate and cracker! The owners are so nice and in terms of location/patio design. <Review>UPDATED REVIEW: Denise contacted me by phone to discuss our experience at Altipiano in January mentioned below. She apologized for her employees behavior and assured me she would talk with her. Denise's heart for customer service and satisfaction shone through during our conversation. She worked immediately to correct the issue. Denise and her husband Peter provide a true family home environment - one of my favorite parts of Altipiano. I am happy to update my rating to 5 stars. I highly recommend visiting. Great wine, beautiful views and excellent customer service.  PREVIOUS REVIEW from January 2019: My husband and I have visited Altipiano Winery for the past four years, and it is one of our favorite wineries to visit in Ramona, due to the quality wines, the beautiful views and the excellent customer service. Today, we brought friends with us to enjoy this experience, and we were highly disappointed. Before could make it through the doorway of the tasting room, the woman working there loudly stated that she will need to check all IDs. She did not say hello, she did not say welcome to our winery, she simply saw us and stated she will need to see IDs (we are in our 40s-50s by the way). I do not mind showing an ID, but her attitude was unwelcoming and unkind - a completely different experience than what I am accustomed to at Altipiano. We showed our IDs and then found a table outside where we could sit. Thank God for Denise Clark today, or we would have walked out. Once we sat at our table, Denise (wine maker and co-owner) asked us how we were doing. Thank you Denise for asking. Your husband usually talks to us, pours our wine, tells jokes and makes us feel at home. Today we felt unwelcome, like strangers, until you visited our table. I hope you will have a talk with the woman working the tasting room, and help her understand how to treat ALL customers with kindness and respect. <GmapID>0x80c2bc890d190c81:0x5c9ebc2f9b628a8f<//GmapID><Response>None</Response>< Text>
Interesting architecture,  definitely feels old school.   Not particularly ornate as the Pantages  theatre in Hollywood,  still has an amazing feel of authenticity.

The Los Angeles Ballet performance of The Nutcracker in December was delightful.  From the balcony, we could see the entire stage come to life.  My kids enjoyed the ballet, especially my 10 year old daughter.

The audio was good, with ample sound for a classical performance. We will visit again for a concert.  Parking was about a mile walk, but we enjoyed walking through the historic UCLA campus.</Text>

<Review>I went to see Tigran Hamasyan play here at Royce Hall and I must say that my experience was rather unfortunate.

I want to point out that while I had a great time at the concert, the staffers at Royce Hall did a relatively terrible job managing the show because while a show is going on, it seems that the ushers let people in as the concert in progress. I understand that this is to let people, who paid for their tickets, in but when it gets to the point that so many people are being let in at 20-30 minute intervals and to the point that the performer himself actually has to stop the concert just to let people take their seats, that just completely ruins the experience for everyone. I truly hope that the staff at Royce Hall is made aware of this because if this is a common practice at the performing center, they should know that letting huge groups of people in during the concert just spoils the performance.
